noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">\xc9\x91\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>: <i lang="eu">euskaldunak</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Basque" title="Help:IPA/Basque">[eus\xcc\xbakaldunak]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">vascos</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[\xcb\x88baskos]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">basques</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[bask]</a></span>)  are an <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Totoricaguena2004_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Totoricaguena2004-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> characterised by the <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque language</a>, a common culture and shared <a href="/wiki/Ancestry" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancestry">ancestry</a> to the ancient <a href="/wiki/Vascones" title="Vascones">Vascones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aquitanians" class="mw-redirect" title="Aquitanians">Aquitanians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-G\xc3\xbcntherValdiosera2015_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G\xc3\xbcntherValdiosera2015-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Basques are indigenous to and primarily inhabit an area traditionally known as the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country</a> (<a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>: <i lang="eu">Euskal Herria</i>), a region that is located around the western end of the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> on the coast of the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a> and straddles parts of north-central <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and south-western <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toclimit-3"><div class="toctext">Society</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Sports_in_the_Basque_Country"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Sports in the Basque Country</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Pelota"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Pelota</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Rural_sports"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Rural sports</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Bull_runs_and_bullock_games"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Bull runs and bullock games</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Football"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Football</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Rugby_union"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">Rugby union</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Professional_cycling"><span class="tocnumber">6.6</span> <span class="toctext">Professional cycling</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Politics"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Politics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Political_conflicts"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Political conflicts</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Language_2"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Language</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Political_status_and_violence"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Political status and violence</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-27"><a href="#Political_violence"><span class="tocnumber">8.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Political violence</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Classification"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Classification</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Genetics"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Genetics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#New_genetic_findings,_2015"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">New genetic findings, 2015</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Notable_Basques"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Notable Basques</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_of_the_word_Basque">Etymology of the word <i>Basque</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology of the word Basque">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barscunes_transparent.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Barscunes_transparent.png/220px-Barscunes_transparent.png" width="220" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Barscunes_transparent.png/330px-Barscunes_transparent.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Barscunes_transparent.png/440px-Barscunes_transparent.png 2x" data-file-width="655" data-file-height="330" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barscunes_transparent.png" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Barscunes coin, Roman period</div></div></div>\n<p>The English word <i>Basque</i> may be pronounced <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">\xc9\x91\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span></span>/</a></span></span> and derives from the French <i>Basque</i> (<small>French pronunciation:&#160;&#8203;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[bask]</a></span>), which is derived from <a href="/wiki/Gascon_language" title="Gascon language">Gascon</a> <i>Basco</i> (pronounced <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xcb\x88basku/</span>), cognate with Spanish <i>Vasco </i>(pronounced <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xcb\x88basko/</span>). These, in turn, come from <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>Vasco</i> (pronounced <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/wasko/</span>), plural <i><a href="/wiki/Vascones" title="Vascones">Vascones</a></i> (see History section below). The Latin <a href="/wiki/Labial-velar_approximant" class="mw-redirect" title="Labial-velar approximant">labial-velar approximant</a> /w/ generally <a href="/wiki/Betacism" title="Betacism">evolved into</a> the <a href="/wiki/Bilabial" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilabial">bilabials</a> /b/ and /\xce\xb2\xcc\x9e/ in Gascon and Spanish, probably under the influence of Basque and <a href="/wiki/Aquitanian_language" title="Aquitanian language">Aquitanian</a>, a language related to old Basque and spoken in <a href="/wiki/Gascony" title="Gascony">Gascony</a> in <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">Antiquity</a> (similarly the Latin /w/ evolved into /v/ in <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> and other languages).\n</p><p>Several coins from the 2nd and 1st centuries BC found in the Basque Country bear the inscription <i>barscunes</i>. The place where they were minted is not certain, but is thought to be somewhere near <a href="/wiki/Pamplona" title="Pamplona">Pamplona</a>, in the heartland of the area that historians believe was inhabited by the <i>Vascones</i>. Some scholars have suggested a Celtic etymology based on <i>bhar-s-</i>, meaning "summit", "point" or "leaves", according to which <i>barscunes</i> may have meant "the mountain people", "the tall ones" or "the proud ones", while others have posited a relationship to a <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">proto-Indo-European</a> root <i>*bar-</i> meaning "border", "frontier", "march".<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Basque, people call themselves the <i>euskaldunak</i>, singular <i>euskaldun</i>, formed from <i>euskal-</i> (i.e. "Basque (language)") and <i>-dun</i> (i.e. "one who has"); <i>euskaldun</i> literally means a Basque speaker. Not all Basques are Basque-speakers. Therefore, the <a href="/wiki/Neologism" title="Neologism">neologism</a> <i>euskotar</i>, plural <i>euskotarrak</i>, was coined in the 19th century to mean a culturally Basque person, whether Basque-speaking or not. Alfonso Irigoyen posits that the word <i>euskara</i> is derived from an ancient Basque verb <i>enautsi</i> "to say" (cf. modern Basque <i>esan</i>) and the suffix <i>-(k)ara</i> ("way (of doing something)"). Thus <i>euskara</i> would literally mean "way of saying", "way of speaking". One item of evidence in favour of this hypothesis is found in the Spanish book <i>Compendio Historial</i>, written in 1571 by the Basque writer <a href="/w/index.php?title=Esteban_de_Garibay&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Esteban de Garibay (page does not exist)">Esteban de Garibay</a>. He records the name of the Basque language as <i>enusquera</i>. It may, however, be a writing mistake.\n</p><p>In the 19th century, the Basque nationalist activist <a href="/wiki/Sabino_Arana" title="Sabino Arana">Sabino Arana</a> posited an original root <i>euzko</i> which, he thought, came from <i>eguzkiko</i> ("of the sun", related to the assumption of an original <a href="/wiki/Solar_deity" title="Solar deity">solar religion</a>). On the basis of this putative root, Arana proposed the name <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Euzkadi</a> for an independent Basque nation, composed of seven Basque historical territories. Arana\'s neologism <i>Euzkadi</i> (in the regularized spelling Euskadi) is still widely used in both Basque and Spanish, since it is now the official name of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous Community">Autonomous Community</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Basque_people" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Basque people">History of the Basque people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_the_Basques" title="Origin of the Basques">Origin of the Basques</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)#History" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country (greater region) \xc2\xa7&#160;History</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_-_Arriv%C3%A9e_des_marchandes_de_sardines_-_Fonds_Ancely_-_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bayonne_-_Arriv%C3%A9e_des_marchandes_de_sardines_-_Fonds_Ancely_-_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Bayonne_-_Arriv%C3%A9e_des_marchandes_de_sardines_-_Fonds_Ancely_-_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bayonne_-_Arriv%C3%A9e_des_marchandes_de_sardines_-_Fonds_Ancely_-_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Bayonne_-_Arriv%C3%A9e_des_marchandes_de_sardines_-_Fonds_Ancely_-_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bayonne_-_Arriv%C3%A9e_des_marchandes_de_sardines_-_Fonds_Ancely_-_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Bayonne_-_Arriv%C3%A9e_des_marchandes_de_sardines_-_Fonds_Ancely_-_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1426" data-file-height="983" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_-_Arriv%C3%A9e_des_marchandes_de_sardines_-_Fonds_Ancely_-_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Basque women in <a href="/wiki/Bayonne" title="Bayonne">Bayonne</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pamplona_-_Monumento_a_los_Fueros_12.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Pamplona_-_Monumento_a_los_Fueros_12.JPG/170px-Pamplona_-_Monumento_a_los_Fueros_12.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Pamplona_-_Monumento_a_los_Fueros_12.JPG/255px-Pamplona_-_Monumento_a_los_Fueros_12.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Pamplona_-_Monumento_a_los_Fueros_12.JPG/340px-Pamplona_-_Monumento_a_los_Fueros_12.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pamplona_-_Monumento_a_los_Fueros_12.JPG" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Monument to the <a href="/wiki/Fuero#Basque_and_Pyrenean_fueros" title="Fuero">Charters</a> in Pamplona (1903)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulgor.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ulgor.jpg/220px-Ulgor.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ulgor.jpg/330px-Ulgor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ulgor.jpg/440px-Ulgor.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="330" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulgor.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Ulgor, earliest nucleus of the cooperative movement and <a href="/wiki/Mondragon_Corporation" title="Mondragon Corporation">MCC</a> (1956)</div></div></div>\n<p>Since the Basque language is unrelated to Indo-European, it has long been thought to represent the people or culture that occupied Europe before the spread of Indo-European languages there. A comprehensive analysis of Basque genetic patterns has shown that Basque genetic uniqueness predates the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">arrival of agriculture</a> in the Iberian Peninsula, about 7,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It is thought that Basques are a remnant of the early inhabitants of Western Europe, specifically those of the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Cantabrian_region" title="Franco-Cantabrian region">Franco-Cantabrian region</a>. Basque tribes were already mentioned in Roman times by Strabo and Pliny, including the <a href="/wiki/Vascones" title="Vascones">Vascones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novempopulania" title="Novempopulania">the Aquitani</a>, and others. There is enough evidence to support the hypothesis that at that time and later they spoke old varieties of the Basque language (see: <a href="/wiki/Aquitanian_language" title="Aquitanian language">Aquitanian language</a>).\n</p><p>In the Early Middle Ages the territory between the <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Garonne" title="Garonne">Garonne</a> rivers was known as <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Vasconia" class="mw-redirect" title="Duchy of Vasconia">Vasconia</a>, a vaguely defined ethnic area and political entity struggling to fend off pressure from the Iberian <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigothic</a> kingdom and <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">Arab rule to the south</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> push from the north.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lewis_AR_20-33_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis_AR_20-33-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> By the turn of the first millennium, the territory of <a href="/wiki/Gascony" title="Gascony">Vasconia</a> had fragmented into different feudal regions, such as <a href="/wiki/Soule" title="Soule">Soule</a> and <a href="/wiki/Labourd" title="Labourd">Labourd</a>, while south of the Pyrenees the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Castile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Pamplona" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Pamplona">Pamplona</a> and the Pyrenean counties of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Aragon" title="County of Aragon">Aragon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sobrarbe" title="Sobrarbe">Sobrarbe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ribagorza" class="mw-redirect" title="Ribagorza">Ribagorza</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">Kingdom of Aragon</a>), and <a href="/wiki/County_of_Pallars" title="County of Pallars">Pallars</a> emerged as the main regional entities with Basque population in the 9th and 10th centuries.\n</p><p>The Kingdom of Pamplona, a central Basque realm, later known as <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Navarre</a>, underwent a process of feudalization and was subject to the influence of its much larger Aragonese, Castilian and French neighbours. Castile deprived Navarre of its coastline by conquering <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">key western territories</a> (1199\xe2\x80\x931201), leaving the kingdom landlocked. The Basques were ravaged by the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Bands" title="War of the Bands">War of the Bands</a>, bitter partisan wars between local ruling families. Weakened by the Navarrese civil war, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Iberian_Navarre" title="Spanish conquest of Iberian Navarre">bulk of the realm eventually fell</a> before the onslaught of the Spanish armies (1512\xe2\x80\x931524). However, <a href="/wiki/Lower_Navarre" title="Lower Navarre">the Navarrese territory north of the Pyrenees</a> remained beyond the reach of an increasingly powerful Spain. <a href="/wiki/Lower_Navarre" title="Lower Navarre">Lower Navarre</a> became a province of France in 1620.\n</p><p>Nevertheless, the Basques enjoyed a great deal of self-government <a href="/wiki/End_of_Basque_home_rule_in_France" title="End of Basque home rule in France">until the French Revolution (1790)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Carlist_Wars" title="Carlist Wars">Carlist Wars</a> (1839, 1876), when the Basques supported heir apparent <a href="/wiki/Infante_Carlos_of_Spain,_Count_of_Molina" class="mw-redirect" title="Infante Carlos of Spain, Count of Molina">Carlos V</a> and his descendants. On either side of the Pyrenees, the Basques <a href="/wiki/End_of_Basque_home_rule_in_Spain" title="End of Basque home rule in Spain">lost their native institutions and laws</a> held during the <i><a href="/wiki/Ancien_r%C3%A9gime" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancien r\xc3\xa9gime">Ancien r\xc3\xa9gime</a></i>. Since then, despite the current limited self-governing status of the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Autonomous Community</a> and Navarre as settled by the Spanish Constitution, many Basques have attempted higher degrees of self-empowerment (see <a href="/wiki/Basque_nationalism" title="Basque nationalism">Basque nationalism</a>), sometimes by acts of violence. <a href="/wiki/Labourd" title="Labourd">Labourd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lower_Navarre" title="Lower Navarre">Lower Navarre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Soule" title="Soule">Soule</a> were integrated into the <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">French department system</a> (starting 1790), with Basque efforts to establish a region-specific political-administrative entity failing to take off to date. However, in January 2017, a single agglomaration community was established for the <a href="/wiki/French_Basque_Country" title="French Basque Country">Basque Country in France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_and_administrative_divisions">Political and administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Political and administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ekialderantz_Urkulutik.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ekialderantz_Urkulutik.JPG/220px-Ekialderantz_Urkulutik.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ekialderantz_Urkulutik.JPG/330px-Ekialderantz_Urkulutik.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ekialderantz_Urkulutik.JPG/440px-Ekialderantz_Urkulutik.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ekialderantz_Urkulutik.JPG" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Mountains of the Basque Country</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leitza.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Leitza.JPG/220px-Leitza.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Leitza.JPG/330px-Leitza.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Leitza.JPG/440px-Leitza.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leitza.JPG" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leitza" title="Leitza">Leitza</a>, in Navarre, Basque Country</div></div></div>\n<p>The Basque region is divided into at least three administrative units, namely the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Autonomous_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Basque Autonomous Community">Basque Autonomous Community</a> and <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">Navarre</a> in Spain, and the <a href="/wiki/Arrondissements_of_France" title="Arrondissements of France">arrondissement</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bayonne" title="Bayonne">Bayonne</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_France" title="Cantons of France">cantons</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maul%C3%A9on-Licharre" title="Maul\xc3\xa9on-Licharre">Maul\xc3\xa9on-Licharre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tardets-Sorholus" title="Tardets-Sorholus">Tardets-Sorholus</a> in the <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partement</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es_Atlantiques" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es Atlantiques">Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es Atlantiques</a>, France.\n</p><p>The autonomous community (a concept established in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a>) known as <i>Euskal Autonomia Erkidegoa</i> or EAE in Basque and as <i>Comunidad Aut\xc3\xb3noma Vasca</i> or CAV in Spanish (in English: <i>Basque Autonomous Community</i> or BAC),<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> is made up of the three Spanish provinces of <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lava" title="\xc3\x81lava">\xc3\x81lava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biscay" title="Biscay">Biscay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gipuzkoa" title="Gipuzkoa">Gipuzkoa</a>. The corresponding Basque names of these territories are <i>Araba</i>, <i>Bizkaia</i> and <i>Gipuzkoa</i>, and their Spanish names are <i>\xc3\x81lava</i>, <i>Vizcaya</i> and <i>Guip\xc3\xbazcoa</i>.\n</p><p>The BAC only includes three of the seven provinces of the currently called historical territories. It is sometimes referred to simply as "the Basque Country" (or <i>Euskadi</i>) by writers and public agencies only considering those three western provinces, but also on occasions merely as a convenient abbreviation when this does not lead to confusion in the context. Others reject this usage as inaccurate and are careful to specify the BAC (or an equivalent expression such as "the three provinces", up to 1978 referred to as "Provincias Vascongadas" in Spanish) when referring to this entity or region. Likewise, terms such as "the Basque Government" for "the government of the BAC" are commonly though not universally employed. In particular in common usage the French term <i>Pays Basque</i> ("Basque Country"), in the absence of further qualification, refers either to the whole <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country</a> ("Euskal Herria" in Basque), or not infrequently to the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Basque_Country" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Basque Country">northern (or "French") Basque Country</a> specifically.\n</p><p>Under Spain\'s present constitution, Navarre (<i>Nafarroa</i> in present-day Basque, <i>Navarra</i> historically in Spanish) constitutes a separate entity, called in present-day Basque <i>Nafarroako Foru Erkidegoa</i>, in Spanish <i>Comunidad Foral de Navarra</i> (the autonomous community of Navarre). The government of this autonomous community is the Government of Navarre. Note that in historical contexts Navarre may refer to a wider area, and that the present-day northern Basque province of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Navarre" title="Lower Navarre">Lower Navarre</a> may also be referred to as (part of) <i>Nafarroa</i>, while the term "High Navarre" (<i>Nafarroa Garaia</i> in Basque, <i>Alta Navarra</i> in Spanish) is also encountered as a way of referring to the territory of the present-day autonomous community.\n</p><p>There are three other historic provinces parts of the Basque Country: <a href="/wiki/Labourd" title="Labourd">Labourd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lower_Navarre" title="Lower Navarre">Lower Navarre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soule" title="Soule">Soule</a> (<i>Lapurdi, Nafarroa Beherea</i> and <i>Zuberoa</i> in Basque; <i>Labourd, Basse-Navarre</i> and <i>Soule</i> in French), devoid of official status within France\'s present-day political and administrative territorial organization, and only minor political support to the Basque nationalists. A large number of regional and local nationalist and non-nationalist representatives have waged a campaign for years advocating for the creation of a separate Basque <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partement</a>, while these demands have gone unheard by the French administration.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Population.2C_main_cities_and_languages"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Population,_main_cities_and_languages">Population, main cities and languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Population, main cities and languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Olentzero,_Beasain.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Olentzero%2C_Beasain.jpg/220px-Olentzero%2C_Beasain.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Olentzero%2C_Beasain.jpg/330px-Olentzero%2C_Beasain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Olentzero%2C_Beasain.jpg/440px-Olentzero%2C_Beasain.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Olentzero,_Beasain.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Olentzero" title="Olentzero">Olentzero</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gipuzkoa" title="Gipuzkoa">Gipuzkoa</a>, Basque Country</div></div></div>\n<p>There are 2,123,000 people living in the Basque Autonomous Community (279,000 in Alava, 1,160,000 in Biscay and 684,000 in Gipuzkoa). The most important cities in this region, which serve as the provinces\' administrative centers, are <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a> (in Biscay), <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n" title="San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n">San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n</a> (in Gipuzkoa) and <a href="/wiki/Vitoria-Gasteiz" title="Vitoria-Gasteiz">Vitoria-Gasteiz</a> (in \xc3\x81lava). The official languages are Basque and Spanish. Knowledge of Spanish is compulsory under the Spanish constitution (article no. 3), and knowledge and usage of Basque is a right under the Statute of Autonomy (article no. 6), so only knowledge of Spanish is virtually universal. Knowledge of Basque, after declining for many years during <a href="/wiki/Spain_under_Franco" class="mw-redirect" title="Spain under Franco">Franco\'s dictatorship</a> owing to official persecution, is again on the rise due to favorable official language policies and popular support. Currently about 33 percent of the population in the Basque Autonomous Community speaks Basque.\n</p><p>Navarre has a population of 601,000; its administrative capital and main city, also regarded by many nationalist Basques as the Basques\' historical capital, is Pamplona (<i>Iru\xc3\xb1ea</i> in modern Basque). Only Spanish is an official language of Navarre, and the Basque language is only co-official in the province\'s northern region, where most Basque-speaking Navarrese are concentrated.\n</p><p>About a quarter of a million people live in the <a href="/wiki/French_Basque_Country" title="French Basque Country">French Basque Country</a>. Nowadays Basque-speakers refer to this region as <i>Iparralde</i> (Basque for North), and to the Spanish provinces as <i>Hegoalde</i> (South). Much of this population lives in or near the Bayonne-Anglet-Biarritz (BAB) urban belt on the coast (in Basque these are <i>Baiona</i>, <i>Angelu</i> and <i>Miarritze</i>). The Basque language, which was traditionally spoken by most of the region\'s population outside the BAB urban zone, is today rapidly losing ground to French. The French Basque Country\'s lack of self-government within the French state is coupled with the absence of official status for the Basque language in the region. Attempts to introduce bilingualism in local administration have so far met direct refusal from French officials.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Basque_diaspora">Basque diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Basque diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Basque_diaspora" title="Basque diaspora">Basque diaspora</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Basque_festival_in_Buenos_Aires_August_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Basque_festival_in_Buenos_Aires_August_2011.jpg/220px-Basque_festival_in_Buenos_Aires_August_2011.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Basque_festival_in_Buenos_Aires_August_2011.jpg/330px-Basque_festival_in_Buenos_Aires_August_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Basque_festival_in_Buenos_Aires_August_2011.jpg/440px-Basque_festival_in_Buenos_Aires_August_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Basque_festival_in_Buenos_Aires_August_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Basque festival in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, Argentina</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Winnemucca_Basque_Festival.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Winnemucca_Basque_Festival.jpg/220px-Winnemucca_Basque_Festival.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Winnemucca_Basque_Festival.jpg/330px-Winnemucca_Basque_Festival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Winnemucca_Basque_Festival.jpg/440px-Winnemucca_Basque_Festival.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Winnemucca_Basque_Festival.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Basque festival in <a href="/wiki/Winnemucca,_Nevada" title="Winnemucca, Nevada">Winnemucca, Nevada</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Large numbers of Basques have left the Basque Country to settle in the rest of Spain, France or other parts of the world in different historical periods, often for economic or political reasons. Historically the Basques abroad were often employed in shepherding and ranching and by maritime fisheries and merchants. Millions of Basque descendants (see <a href="/wiki/Basque_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Basque American">Basque American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basque_Canadian" class="mw-redirect" title="Basque Canadian">Basque Canadian</a>) live in North America (the United States; Canada, mainly in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>), Latin America (in all 23 countries), South Africa, and Australia.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Unamuno" title="Miguel de Unamuno">Miguel de Unamuno</a> said: "There are at least two things that clearly can be attributed to Basques: the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Chile">Republic of Chile</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Chilean historian Luis Thayer Ojeda estimated that 48 percent of immigrants to Chile in the 17th and 18th centuries were Basque.<sup id="cite_ref-DouglassBilbao2005_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DouglassBilbao2005-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Estimates range between 2.5 - 5&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Basque_Chilean" class="mw-redirect" title="Basque Chilean">Basque descendants</a> live in <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>; the Basque have been a major if not the strongest influence in the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Cultural" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural">cultural</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic">economic</a> development.\n</p><p>Basque place names are to be found, such as <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Vizcaya,_New_Spain" title="Nueva Vizcaya, New Spain">Nueva Vizcaya</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Chihuahua_(state)" title="Chihuahua (state)">Chihuahua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Durango" title="Durango">Durango</a>, Mexico), <a href="/wiki/Biscayne_Bay" title="Biscayne Bay">Biscayne Bay</a> (Guatemala), and <a href="/wiki/Aguereberry_Point" title="Aguereberry Point">Aguereberry Point</a> (United States).<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Nueva Vizcaya was the first province in the north of the Viceroyalty of New Spain (Mexico) to be explored and settled by the Spanish. It consisted mostly of the area which is today the states of Chihuahua and Durango.\n</p><p>In Mexico most Basques are concentrated in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Monterrey" title="Monterrey">Monterrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saltillo" title="Saltillo">Saltillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reynosa" title="Reynosa">Reynosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camargo,_Chihuahua" title="Camargo, Chihuahua">Camargo</a>, and the states of <a href="/wiki/Jalisco" title="Jalisco">Jalisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Durango" title="Durango">Durango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Le%C3%B3n" title="Nuevo Le\xc3\xb3n">Nuevo Le\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamaulipas" title="Tamaulipas">Tamaulipas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coahuila" title="Coahuila">Coahuila</a>. The Basques were important in the mining industry; many were ranchers and vaqueros (<a href="/wiki/Cowboy" title="Cowboy">cowboys</a>), and the rest opened small shops in major cities such as <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadalajara,_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Guadalajara, Mexico">Guadalajara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a>, most Basques have been concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Sacatepequez_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacatepequez Department">Sacatepequez Department</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antigua_Guatemala" title="Antigua Guatemala">Antigua Guatemala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jalapa_Department" title="Jalapa Department">Jalapa</a> for six generations now, while some have migrated to <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_City" title="Guatemala City">Guatemala City</a>.\n</p><p>In Colombia, Basques settled mainly in <a href="/wiki/Antioquia_Department" title="Antioquia Department">Antioquia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_coffee_growing_axis" title="Colombian coffee growing axis">Coffee Axis</a>. It is estimated that nearly 2,500,000 persons from all Antioquia (40% of this <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Colombia" title="Departments of Colombia">department</a>) have Basque ancestry, as well, in the 19th century about 10% of Colombia\'s total population were Basque descendants.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (November 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Antioquia has one of the biggest concentrations of Basques descendants around the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 1955, Joaqu\xc3\xadn Ospina said: "Is there something more similar to the Basque people than the "<i>antioque\xc3\xb1os</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Also, writer Arturo Escobar Uribe said in his book "<i>Mitos de Antioquia</i>" (Myths of Antioquia) (1950): "Antioquia, which in its clean ascendance predominates the peninsular farmer of the Basque provinces, inherited the virtues of its ancestors... Despite the predominance of the white race, its extension in the mountains... has projected over Colombia\'s map the prototype of its race; in <a href="/wiki/Medell%C3%ADn" title="Medell\xc3\xadn">Medell\xc3\xadn</a> with the industrial <a href="/wiki/Paisa_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Paisa region">paisa</a>, entrepreneur, strong and steady... in its towns, the adventurer, arrogant, world-explorer... Its myths, which are an evidence of their deep credulity and an indubitable proof of their Iberian ancestor, are the sequel of the conqueror\'s blood which runs through their veins...".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bambuco" title="Bambuco">Bambuco</a>, a Colombian folk music, has Basque roots.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest of several important Basque communities in the United States is in the area around <a href="/wiki/Boise,_Idaho" title="Boise, Idaho">Boise, Idaho</a>, home to the Basque Museum and Cultural Center, host to an annual Basque festival, as well as a festival for the Basque diaspora every five years. <a href="/wiki/Reno,_Nevada" title="Reno, Nevada">Reno, Nevada</a>, where the Center for Basque Studies and the Basque Studies Library are located at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nevada,_Reno" title="University of Nevada, Reno">University of Nevada</a>, is another significant nucleus of Basque population. <a href="/wiki/Elko,_Nevada" title="Elko, Nevada">Elko, Nevada</a> sponsors an annual Basque festival that celebrates the dance, cuisine and cultures of the Basque peoples of Spanish, French and Mexican nationalities who have arrived in <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a> since the late 19th century.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> has a large percentage of Hispanics descended from Basques who participated in the conquest of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>. Many of the original <a href="/wiki/Tejano" title="Tejano">Tejanos</a> had Basque blood, including those who fought in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Alamo" title="Battle of the Alamo">Battle of the Alamo</a> alongside many of the other Texans. Along the Mexican/Texan border, many Basque surnames can be found. The largest concentration of Basques who settled on Mexico\'s north-eastern "frontera", including the states of <a href="/wiki/Chihuahua_(state)" title="Chihuahua (state)">Chihuahua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Durango" title="Durango">Durango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coahuila" title="Coahuila">Coahuila</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Le%C3%B3n" title="Nuevo Le\xc3\xb3n">Nuevo Le\xc3\xb3n</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tamaulipas" title="Tamaulipas">Tamaulipas</a>, also settled along Texas\' <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Grande River">Rio Grande River</a> from <a href="/wiki/South_Texas" title="South Texas">South Texas</a> to <a href="/wiki/West_Texas" title="West Texas">West Texas</a>. Many of the historic <i>hidalgos</i>, or noble families from this area, had gained their titles and land grants from Spain and Mexico; they still value their land. Some of North America\'s largest ranches, which were founded under these colonial land grants, can be found in this region.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> has a major concentration of Basques, most notably in the <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_Valley" title="San Joaquin Valley">San Joaquin Valley</a> between <a href="/wiki/Stockton,_California" title="Stockton, California">Stockton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fresno,_California" title="Fresno, California">Fresno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bakersfield,_California" title="Bakersfield, California">Bakersfield</a>. The city of Bakersfield has a large Basque community and the city has several Basque restaurants, including Noriega\'s which won the 2011 James Beard Foundation America\'s Classic Award. There is a history of Basque culture in <a href="/wiki/Chino,_California" title="Chino, California">Chino, California</a>. In Chino, two annual Basque festivals celebrate the dance, cuisine, and culture of the peoples. The surrounding area of <a href="/wiki/San_Bernardino_County,_California" title="San Bernardino County, California">San Bernardino County</a> has many Basque descendants as residents. They are mostly descendants of settlers from Spain and Mexico. These Basques in California are grouped in the group known as <i><a href="/wiki/Californio" title="Californio">Californios</a></i>.\n</p><p>Basques of European Spanish-French and Latin American nationalities also settled throughout the western U.S. in states like <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="vertical-navbox Basques">History of the Basques</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead"
