data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="670" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nortasun.png" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Cultural identity according to the 1981 and 1991 census based on the question <i>Do you consider yourself Basque?</i> &#160;&#160;1&#160;-&#160;Yes<br />2&#160;-&#160;Yes, in some ways &#160;&#160;3&#160;-&#160;No<br />4&#160;-&#160;Don\'t know / Don\'t answer</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque language</a></div><p>\nThe identifying language of the Basques is called Basque or <i>Euskara</i>, spoken today by 25%-30%<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> of the region\'s population. An idea of the central place of the cultural terms in Basque nationalist politicians is given by the fact that, in Basque, Basques identify themselves by the term <i>euskaldun</i> and their country as <i>Euskal Herria</i>, literally "Basque speaker" and "Country of the Basque Language" respectively. The language has been made a political issue by official Spanish and French policies restricting its use either historically or currently; however, this has not stopped the teaching, speaking, writing, and cultivating of this increasingly vibrant minority language. This sense of Basque identity tied to the local language does not exist in isolation. It is juxtaposed with an equally strong sense of national identity tied with the use of the Spanish and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French languages</a> among other Basques. As with many European states, a regional identity, be it linguistically derived or otherwise, is not mutually exclusive with the broader national one. For example, Basque <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_union_team" title="France national rugby union team">rugby union</a> player for France, <a href="/wiki/Imanol_Harinordoquy" title="Imanol Harinordoquy">Imanol Harinordoquy</a>, has said about his national identity:</p><blockquote><p>I am French and Basque. There is no conflict, I am proud of both. . . . I have friends who are involved in the political side of things but that is not for me. My only interest is the culture, the Euskera language, the people, our history and ways.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>As a result of state language promotion, school policies, the effects of mass media and migration, today virtually all Basques (except for some children below school age) speak the official language of their state (Spanish or French). There are extremely few Basque monolingual speakers: essentially all Basque speakers are bilingual on both sides of the border. Spanish or French is typically the first language of citizens from other regions (who often feel no need to learn Basque), and Spanish or French is also the first language of many Basques, all of which maintains the dominance of the state tongues of both France and Spain. Recent Basque Government policies aim to change this pattern, as they are viewed as potential threats against mainstream usage of the minority tongue.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Basque language is thought to be a <a href="/wiki/Genetic_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Genetic (linguistics)">genetic</a> <a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">language isolate</a> in contrast with other European languages, almost all of which belong to the broad <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_language_family" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-European language family">Indo-European language family</a>. Another peculiarity of Basque is that it has been spoken continuously <i><a href="/wiki/In_situ" title="In situ">in situ</a></i>, in and around its present territorial location, for longer than other modern European languages, which were all introduced in historic or prehistoric times through population migrations or other processes of cultural transmission.<sup id="cite_ref-Trask1997_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trask1997-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (November 2010)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>However, popular stereotypes characterizing Basque as "the oldest language in Europe" and "unique among the world\'s languages" may be misunderstood and lead to erroneous assumptions.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Over the centuries, Basque has remained in continuous contact with neighboring western European languages with which it has come to share numerous lexical properties and typological features; it is therefore misleading to exaggerate the "outlandish" character of Basque. Basque is also a modern language, and is established as a written and printed one used in present-day forms of publication and communication, as well as a language spoken and used in a very wide range of social and cultural contexts, styles, and registers.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_and_inheritance">Land and inheritance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Land and inheritance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ArangurenDorretxea.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/ArangurenDorretxea.jpg/220px-ArangurenDorretxea.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/ArangurenDorretxea.jpg/330px-ArangurenDorretxea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/ArangurenDorretxea.jpg/440px-ArangurenDorretxea.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1608" data-file-height="959" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ArangurenDorretxea.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>The Aranguren baserri in <a href="/wiki/Orozko" title="Orozko">Orozko</a>, converted from a fortified tower</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BaserriLizarralde.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/BaserriLizarralde.jpg/220px-BaserriLizarralde.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/BaserriLizarralde.jpg/330px-BaserriLizarralde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/BaserriLizarralde.jpg/440px-BaserriLizarralde.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1678" data-file-height="991" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BaserriLizarralde.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>The Lizarralde baserri (<a href="/wiki/Bergara" title="Bergara">Bergara</a>)</div></div></div>\n<p>Basques have a close attachment to their home (<i>etxe(a)</i> \'house, home\'), especially when this consists of the traditional self-sufficient, family-run farm or <i><a href="/wiki/Baserri" title="Baserri">baserri</a>(a)</i>. Home in this context is synonymous with family roots. Some <a href="/wiki/Basque_surnames" title="Basque surnames">Basque surnames</a> were adapted from old <i>baserri</i> or <a href="/wiki/Habitation_name" class="mw-redirect" title="Habitation name">habitation names</a>. They typically related to a geographical orientation or other locally meaningful identifying features. Such surnames provide even those Basques whose families may have left the land generations ago with an important link to their rural family origins: <i>Bengoetxea</i> "the house of further down", <i>Goikoetxea</i> "the house above", <i>Landaburu</i> "top of the field", <i>Errekondo</i> "next to the stream", <i>Elizalde</i> "by the church", <i>Mendizabal</i> "wide hill", <i>Usetxe</i> "house of birds" <i>Ibarretxe</i> "house in the valley", <i>Etxeberria</i> "the new house", and so on.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In contrast to surrounding regions, ancient Basque inheritance patterns, recognised in the <i><a href="/wiki/Fueros" class="mw-redirect" title="Fueros">fueros</a>,</i> favoured survival of the unity of inherited land holdings. In a kind of primogeniture, these usually were inherited by either the eldest male or female. As in other cultures, the fate of other family members depended on the assets of a family: wealthy Basque families tended to provide for all children in some way, while less-affluent may have had only one asset to provide to one child. However, this heir often provided for the rest of the family (unlike in England, with strict primogeniture, where the eldest son inherited everything and often did not provide for others). Even though they were provided for in some way, younger siblings had to make much of their living by other means. Before the advent of industrialisation, this system resulted in the emigration of many rural Basques to Spain, France or the Americas. Harsh by modern standards, this custom resulted in a great many enterprising figures of Basque origin who went into the world to earn their way, from Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistadors</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Lope_de_Aguirre" title="Lope de Aguirre">Lope de Aguirre</a> and Francisco V\xc3\xa1squez de Coronado, to explorers, missionaries and saints of the Catholic Church, such as <a href="/wiki/Francis_Xavier" title="Francis Xavier">Francis Xavier</a>.\n</p><p>A widespread belief that Basque society was originally <a href="/wiki/Matriarchal" class="mw-redirect" title="Matriarchal">matriarchal</a> is at odds with the current, clearly <a href="/wiki/Patrilineal" class="mw-redirect" title="Patrilineal">patrilineal</a> kinship system and inheritance structures. Some scholars and commentators have attempted to reconcile these points by assuming that patrilineal kinship represents an innovation. In any case, the social position of women in both traditional and modern Basque society is somewhat better than in neighbouring cultures, and women have a substantial influence in decisions about the domestic economy. In the past, some women participated in collective magical ceremonies. They were key participants in a rich folklore, today largely forgotten.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Basque_cuisine" title="Basque cuisine">Basque cuisine</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Basque_cuisine" title="Basque cuisine">Basque cuisine</a> is at the heart of Basque culture, influenced by the neighboring communities and the excellent produce from the sea and the land. A 20th-century feature of Basque culture is the phenomenon of <a href="/wiki/Gastronomical_society" class="mw-redirect" title="Gastronomical society">gastronomical societies</a> (called <i><a href="/wiki/Txoko" title="Txoko">txoko</a></i> in Basque), food clubs where men gather to cook and enjoy their own food. Until recently, women were allowed entry only one day in the year. Cider houses (<a href="/wiki/Sagardotegi" title="Sagardotegi">Sagardotegiak</a>) are popular restaurants in Gipuzkoa open for a few months while the cider is in season.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_production">Cultural production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cultural production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Artzaiak_inudeak_2009_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Artzaiak_inudeak_2009_001.jpg/220px-Artzaiak_inudeak_2009_001.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Artzaiak_inudeak_2009_001.jpg/330px-Artzaiak_inudeak_2009_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Artzaiak_inudeak_2009_001.jpg/440px-Artzaiak_inudeak_2009_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2336" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Artzaiak_inudeak_2009_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Artzaiak eta inudeak festival, <a href="/wiki/Donostia" class="mw-redirect" title="Donostia">Donostia</a>, Basque Country.</div></div></div>\n<p>At the end of the 20th century, despite <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a> violence (ended in 2010) and the crisis of heavy industries, the Basque economic condition recovered remarkably. They emerged from the <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Franco</a> regime with a revitalized language and culture. The Basque language expanded geographically led by large increases in the major urban centers of Pamplona, Bilbao, and Bayonne, where only a few decades ago the Basque language had all but disappeared. Nowadays, the number of Basque speakers is maintaining its level or increasing slightly.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Basque_music" title="Basque music">Basque music</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Basque_dance.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Basque_dance.JPG/220px-Basque_dance.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Basque_dance.JPG/330px-Basque_dance.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Basque_dance.JPG/440px-Basque_dance.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Basque_dance.JPG" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Basque dance</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Traditionally Basques have been mostly <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholics</a>. In the 19th century and well into the 20th, Basques as a group remained notably devout and churchgoing. In recent years church attendance has fallen off, as in most of Western Europe. The region has been a source of missionaries like <a href="/wiki/Francis_Xavier" title="Francis Xavier">Francis Xavier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michel_Garico%C3%AFts" title="Michel Garico\xc3\xafts">Michel Garico\xc3\xafts</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ignatius_Loyola" class="mw-redirect" title="Ignatius Loyola">Ignatius Loyola</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a>, was a Basque. <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> <a href="/wiki/Franciscan" class="mw-redirect" title="Franciscan">Franciscan</a> <a href="/wiki/Ferm%C3%ADn_Lasu%C3%A9n" title="Ferm\xc3\xadn Lasu\xc3\xa9n">Ferm\xc3\xadn Lasu\xc3\xa9n</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Vitoria-Gasteiz" title="Vitoria-Gasteiz">Vitoria</a>. Lasu\xc3\xa9n was the successor to Franciscan Padre <a href="/wiki/Jun%C3%ADpero_Serra" title="Jun\xc3\xadpero Serra">Jun\xc3\xadpero Serra</a> and founded 9 of the 21 extant <a href="/wiki/California_Missions" class="mw-redirect" title="California Missions">California Missions</a> along the coast.\n</p><p>A sprout of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> in the continental Basque Country produced the first translation of the new Testament into Basque by <a href="/wiki/Joanes_Leizarraga" title="Joanes Leizarraga">Joanes Leizarraga</a>. Queen <a href="/wiki/Jeanne_III_of_Navarre" class="mw-redirect" title="Jeanne III of Navarre">Jeanne III of Navarre</a>, a devout <a href="/wiki/Huguenot" class="mw-redirect" title="Huguenot">Huguenot</a>, commissioned the translation of the New Testament into Basque and B\xc3\xa9arnese for the benefit of her subjects. By the time <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France" title="Henry IV of France">Henry III of Navarre</a> converted to Catholicism in order to become king of France, Protestantism virtually disappeared from the Basque community.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bayonne" title="Bayonne">Bayonne</a> held a Jewish community composed mainly of <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardi Jews</a> fleeing from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Inquisition" title="Portuguese Inquisition">Portuguese Inquisitions</a>. There were also important Jewish and <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> communities in <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">Navarre</a> before the Castilian invasion of 1512-21.\n</p><p>Nowadays, according to one single opinion poll, only slightly more than 50% of Basques profess some kind of belief in <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a>, while the rest are either <a href="/wiki/Agnostic" class="mw-redirect" title="Agnostic">agnostic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Atheist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheist">atheist</a>. The number of religious skeptics increases noticeably for the younger generations, while the older ones are more religious.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a> is, by far, the largest religion in <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a>. In 2012, the proportion of Basques that identify themselves as Catholic was 58.6%,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> while it is one of the most secularized communities of Spain: 24.6% were non-religious and 12.3% of Basques were <a href="/wiki/Atheist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheist">atheist</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Christian_religion_and_mythology">Pre-Christian religion and mythology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Pre-Christian religion and mythology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Basque_mythology" title="Basque mythology">Basque mythology</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-More_footnotes" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/60px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/80px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article includes a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">list of references</a>, but <b>its sources remain unclear</b> because it has <b>insufficient <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">inline citations</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Fact_and_Reference_Check" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Fact and Reference Check">improve</a> this article by <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:When_to_cite" title="Wikipedia:When to cite">introducing</a> more precise citations.</span>  <small><i>(February 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amboto_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Amboto_01.jpg/220px-Amboto_01.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Amboto_01.jpg/330px-Amboto_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Amboto_01.jpg/440px-Amboto_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4067" data-file-height="2933" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amboto_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Anboto" title="Anboto">Anboto</a> mountain is one of sites where <a href="/wiki/Mari_(goddess)" title="Mari (goddess)">Mari</a> was believed to dwell</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dolmen_de_Sorginetxe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Dolmen_de_Sorginetxe.jpg/220px-Dolmen_de_Sorginetxe.jpg" width="220" height="338" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Dolmen_de_Sorginetxe.jpg/330px-Dolmen_de_Sorginetxe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Dolmen_de_Sorginetxe.jpg/440px-Dolmen_de_Sorginetxe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2616" data-file-height="4016" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dolmen_de_Sorginetxe.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Sorginetxe dolmen next to the stream and cave Lezao, home to legends featuring mythological character <a href="/wiki/Mari_(goddess)" title="Mari (goddess)">Mari</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Christianization" title="Christianization">Christianisation</a> of the Basque Country has been the topic of some discussion. There are broadly speaking two views. According to one, Christianity arrived in the Basque Country during the 4th and 5th centuries but according to the other, it did not take place until the 12th and 13th centuries. The main issue lies in the different interpretations of what is considered Christianisation. Early traces of Christianity can be found in the major urban areas from the 4th century onwards, a bishopric from 589 in Pamplona and three hermit cave concentrations (two in \xc3\x81lava, one in Navarre) were in use from the 6th century onwards. In this sense, Christianity arrived "early".\n</p><p>Pre-Christian belief seems to have focused on a goddess called <a href="/wiki/Mari_(goddess)" title="Mari (goddess)">Mari</a>. A number of place-names contain her name and would suggest these places were related to worship of her such as <i><a href="/wiki/Anbotoko_Mari" class="mw-redirect" title="Anbotoko Mari">Anbotoko Mari</a></i> who appears to have been related to the weather. According to one tradition, she travelled every seven years between a cave on Mount <a href="/wiki/Anboto" title="Anboto">Anboto</a> and one on another mountain (the stories vary); the weather would be wet when she was in Anboto, dry when she was in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alo%C3%B1a&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alo\xc3\xb1a (page does not exist)">Alo\xc3\xb1a</a>, or <a href="/w/index.php?title=Supelegor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Supelegor (page does not exist)">Supelegor</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Gorbea" title="Gorbea">Gorbea</a>. One of her names, <i>Mari Urraca</i> possibly ties her to an historical Navarrese princess of the 11th and 12th century, with other legends giving her a brother or cousin who was a Catholic priest. So far the discussions about whether the name Mari is original and just happened to coincide closely with the Christian name Mar\xc3\xada or if Mari is an early Basque attempt to give a Christian veneer to pagan worship have remained speculative. At any rate, Mari (Andramari) is one of the oldest worshipped Christian icons in Basque territories.\n</p><p>Mari\'s consort is <a href="/wiki/Sugaar" title="Sugaar">Sugaar</a>. This <a href="/wiki/Chthonic" title="Chthonic">chthonic</a> couple seem to bear the superior ethical power and also the power of creation and destruction. It\'s said that when they gathered in the high caves of the sacred peaks, they engendered the storms. These meetings typically happened on Friday nights, the day of historical <a href="/wiki/Akelarre_(witchcraft)" class="mw-redirect" title="Akelarre (witchcraft)">akelarre</a> or <a href="/wiki/Coven" title="Coven">coven</a>. Mari was said to reside in Mount <a href="/wiki/Anboto" title="Anboto">Anboto</a>; periodically she crossed the skies as a bright light to reach her other home at mount <a href="/wiki/Txindoki" title="Txindoki">Txindoki</a>.\n</p><p>Legends also speak of many and abundant genies, like <i><a href="/wiki/Jentilak" class="mw-redirect" title="Jentilak">jentilak</a></i> (equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Giant_(mythology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Giant (mythology)">giants</a>), <i>lamiak</i> (equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Nymph" title="Nymph">nymphs</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/Mairu" title="Mairu">mairuak</a></i> (builders of the cromlechs or stone circles, literally <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>), <i>iratxoak</i> (<a href="/wiki/Imp" title="Imp">imps</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/Sorginak" title="Sorginak">sorginak</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Witch" class="mw-redirect" title="Witch">witches</a>, priestess of Mari), and so on. <a href="/wiki/Basajaun" title="Basajaun">Basajaun</a> is a Basque version of the <a href="/wiki/Woodwose" class="mw-redirect" title="Woodwose">Woodwose</a>. This character is probably an anthropomorphism of the bear. There is a <a href="/wiki/Trickster" title="Trickster">trickster</a> named <i><a href="/wiki/San_Martin_Txiki" title="San Martin Txiki">San Martin Txiki</a></i> ("St Martin the Lesser").\n</p><p>It has been shown that some of these stories have entered Basque culture in recent centuries or as part of Roman <i><a href="/wiki/Superstition" title="Superstition">superstition</a></i>. It is unclear whether <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">neolithic</a> stone structures called <a href="/wiki/Dolmen" title="Dolmen">dolmens</a> have a religious significance or were built to house animals or resting shepherds. Some of the dolmens and <a href="/wiki/Stone_circles" class="mw-redirect" title="Stone circles">cromlechs</a> are burial sites serving as well as border markers.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ioaldunak_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Ioaldunak_001.jpg/220px-Ioaldunak_001.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Ioaldunak_001.jpg/330px-Ioaldunak_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Ioaldunak_001.jpg/440px-Ioaldunak_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ioaldunak_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div><i>Ioaldunak</i> dancers of Navarre.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <i>jentilak</i> (\'<a href="/wiki/Giant_(mythology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Giant (mythology)">Giants</a>\'), on the other hand, are a legendary people which explains the disappearance of a people of <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a> culture that used to live in the high lands and with no knowledge of the iron. Many legends about them tell that they were bigger and taller, with a great force, but were displaced by the <i>ferrons</i>, or workers of ironworks foundries, until their total fade-out. They were pagans, but one of them, <a href="/wiki/Olentzero" title="Olentzero">Olentzero</a>, accepted Christianity and became a sort of Basque <a href="/wiki/Santa_Claus" title="Santa Claus">Santa Claus</a>. They gave name to several toponyms, as <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jentilbaratza&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jentilbaratza (page does not exist)">Jentilbaratza</a></i>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Weiditz_Trachtenbuch_125-126.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Weiditz_Trachtenbuch_125-126.jpg/220px-Weiditz_Trachtenbuch_125-126.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Weiditz_Trachtenbuch_125-126.jpg/330px-Weiditz_Trachtenbuch_125-126.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Weiditz_Trachtenbuch_125-126.jpg/440px-Weiditz_Trachtenbuch_125-126.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2647" data-file-height="1778" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Weiditz_Trachtenbuch_125-126.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Senior Basque women during the 16th century; the attire was forbidden on <a href="/wiki/Pierre_de_Lancre" title="Pierre de Lancre">Pierre de Lancre</a>\'s intervention in the Basque Country (1609-1612)</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Historically, Basque society can be described as being somewhat at odds with Roman and later European societal norms.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a>\'s account of the north of Spain in his <i><a href="/wiki/Geographica" title="Geographica">Geographica</a></i> (written between approximately 20 BC and 20 AD) makes a mention of "a sort of woman-rule\xe2\x80\x94not at all a mark of civilization" (Hadington 1992), a first mention of the\xe2\x80\x94for the period\xe2\x80\x94unusual position of women. "Women could inherit and control property as well as officiate in churches. Combined with the issue of lingering pagan beliefs, this enraged the leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Spanish Inquisition</a>, perhaps leading to <a href="/wiki/Logro%C3%B1o_trials" class="mw-redirect" title="Logro\xc3\xb1o trials">one of the largest witch hunts</a> in the Basque town of <a href="/wiki/Logro%C3%B1o" title="Logro\xc3\xb1o">Logro\xc3\xb1o</a> in 1610".<sup id="cite_ref-Hadingham_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hadingham-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This preference for female dominance existed well into the 20th century:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>...<a href="/wiki/Matrilineal" class="mw-redirect" title="Matrilineal">matrilineal</a> inheritance laws, and agricultural work performed by women continued in Basque country until the early twentieth century. For more than a century, scholars have widely discussed the high status of Basque women in law codes, as well as their positions as judges, inheritors, and arbitrators through ante-Roman, medieval, and modern times. The system of laws governing succession in the French Basque region reflected total equality between the sexes. Up until the eve of the French Revolution, the Basque woman was truly \xe2\x80\x98the mistress of the house\', hereditary guardian, and head of the lineage.<sup id="cite_ref-treilo_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treilo-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Although the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">kingdom of Navarre</a> did adopt feudalism, most Basques also possessed unusual social institutions different from those of the rest of feudal Europe. Some aspects of this include the <a href="/wiki/Elizate" title="Elizate">elizate</a> tradition where local house-owners met in front of the church to elect a representative to send to the <i>juntas</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Juntas_Generales" title="Juntas Generales">Juntas Generales</a></i> (such as the <i>Juntas Generales de Vizcaya</i> or <i>Guip\xc3\xbazcoa</i>) which administered much larger areas. Another example was the fact that in the medieval period most land was owned by the farmers, not the Church or a king.<sup id="cite_ref-Trask1997_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trask1997-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (November 2010)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-oprmay_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oprmay-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_in_the_Basque_Country">Sports in the Basque Country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sports in the Basque Country">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LuxioApustua.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/LuxioApustua.jpg/220px-LuxioApustua.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/LuxioApustua.jpg/330px-LuxioApustua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/LuxioApustua.jpg/440px-LuxioApustua.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1624" data-file-height="958" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LuxioApustua.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Rivalry and betting in a <a href="/wiki/Aizkolaritza" title="Aizkolaritza">wood-chopping contest (1949)</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pelota">Pelota</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Pelota">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Basque_pelota" title="Basque pelota">Basque pelota</a></div>\n<p>The great family of ball games has its unique offspring among Basque ball games, known generically as <a href="/wiki/Pilota" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilota">pilota</a> (Spanish: <i>pelota</i>). Some variants have been exported to the United States and <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> under the name of <a href="/wiki/Jai_Alai" class="mw-redirect" title="Jai Alai">Jai Alai</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rural_sports">Rural sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Rural sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Remo-ria-de-bilbao.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Remo-ria-de-bilbao.jpg/220px-Remo-ria-de-bilbao.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Remo-ria-de-bilbao.jpg/330px-Remo-ria-de-bilbao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Remo-ria-de-bilbao.jpg/440px-Remo-ria-de-bilbao.jpg 2x" data-file-width="648" data-file-height="486" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Remo-ria-de-bilbao.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div><i>Trainerilla</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Estuary_of_Bilbao" title="Estuary of Bilbao">Bilbao estuary</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20060122_barrenak_gora.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/20060122_barrenak_gora.jpg/220px-20060122_barrenak_gora.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/20060122_barrenak_gora.jpg/330px-20060122_barrenak_gora.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/20060122_barrenak_gora.jpg/440px-20060122_barrenak_gora.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2001" data-file-height="1485" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20060122_barrenak_gora.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div><i>Barrenatzaileak</i> in <a href="/wiki/Barakaldo" title="Barakaldo">Barakaldo</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Basque_rural_sports" title="Basque rural sports">Basque rural sports</a></div>\n<p>There are several sports derived by Basques from everyday chores. Heavy workers were challenged and bets placed upon them. Examples are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Estropadak" class="mw-redirect" title="Estropadak">estropadak</a></i> rowing regattas: from fishermen activities.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Basque_rural_sports#Sokatira_(tug-of-war)" title="Basque rural sports">sokatira</a></i>: tug-of-war.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Harri-jasotzaileak" title="Harri-jasotzaileak">harri-jasotzea</a></i>: stone-lifting, from quarry works.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Aizkolaritza" title="Aizkolaritza">aizkolaritza</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Basque_rural_sports#Trontza_(sawing)" title="Basque rural sports">trontzalaritza</a></i>: wood-chopping and log sawing.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Basque_rural_sports#Sega_jokoa_(scything)" title="Basque rural sports">sega jokoa</a></i>: cutting grass with a <a href="/wiki/Scythe" title="Scythe">scythe</a>.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Basque_rural_sports#Giza-abere_probak_(dragging_games)" title="Basque rural sports">Giza-abere probak</a></i>: stone block pulling, from construction works:\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Idi_probak" title="Idi probak">idi probak</a></i> with teams of oxen.</li>\n<li><i>asto probak</i> with donkeys.</li>\n<li><i>zaldi probak</i> with horses.</li>\n<li><i>gizon probak</i> with human teams.</li></ul></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Basque_rural_sports#Txinga_eramatea_(weight_carrying)" title="Basque rural sports">txinga eramatea</a></i>: carrying of weights, one in each hand, representing milk canisters.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Basque_rural_sports#Ahari_topeka_(ram_fighting)" title="Basque rural sports">ahari topaketa</a>: ram fights.</i></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Basque_rural_sports#Harri_zulaketa_(hole_drilling)" title="Basque rural sports">harri zulaketa</a></i> competitions: drilling stone blocks with a metal bar, only in the former mining areas of West Biscay.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Basque_rural_sports#Txakur_probak_(sheepdog_trials)" title="Basque rural sports">Basque sheepdog trials</a> competitions.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bull_runs_and_bullock_games">Bull runs and bullock games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Bull runs and bullock games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Encierro" class="mw-redirect" title="Encierro">encierro</a> (bull run) in <a href="/wiki/Pamplona" title="Pamplona">Pamplona</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">fiestas</a> <i><a href="/wiki/San_Ferm%C3%ADn" title="San Ferm\xc3\xadn">Sanfermines</a></i> started as a transport of bulls to the ring. These encierros, as well as other bull and <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">bullock</a> related activities are not exclusive to Pamplona but are traditional in many towns and villages of the Basque country.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_national_football_team" title="Basque Country national football team">Basque Country national football team</a></div>\n<p>There are several clubs within the Basque Country, such as <a href="/wiki/Athletic_Bilbao" title="Athletic Bilbao">Athletic Bilbao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Real_Sociedad" title="Real Sociedad">Real Sociedad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_Alav%C3%A9s" title="Deportivo Alav\xc3\xa9s">Deportivo Alav\xc3\xa9s</a>, <a href="/wiki/SD_Eibar" title="SD Eibar">SD Eibar</a> and, as Navarre club, the <a href="/wiki/CA_Osasuna" title="CA Osasuna">CA Osasuna</a> (the only club in <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> that has a Basque name \xe2\x80\x94 <i>osasuna</i> means "health"). In the 2016-2017 season these five clubs played together in La Liga, the first instance where five Basque clubs have reached that level at the same time. Athletic\'s <a href="/wiki/Athletic_Bilbao_signing_policy" title="Athletic Bilbao signing policy">recruitment policy</a> has meant the club refuses to sign any non-Basque players.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Real Sociedad also previously employed such a policy.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_union">Rugby union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rugby union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> is a popular sport among French Basques, with major clubs <a href="/wiki/Biarritz_Olympique" title="Biarritz Olympique">Biarritz Olympique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aviron_Bayonnais" title="Aviron Bayonnais">Aviron Bayonnais</a> traditional powerhouses in the premier division of French Rugby (the <a href="/wiki/Top_14" title="Top 14">Top 14</a>). Biarritz regularly play <a href="/wiki/Heineken_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Heineken Cup">Heineken Cup</a> matches, especially knockout matches, at <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Anoeta" class="mw-redirect" title="Estadio Anoeta">Estadio Anoeta</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n" title="San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n">San Sebastian</a>. Games between the Basque clubs and Catalan club <a href="/wiki/USA_Perpignan" title="USA Perpignan">USA Perpignan</a> are always hard fought.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_cycling">Professional cycling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Professional cycling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Cycling is popular and the <a href="/wiki/Euskaltel-Euskadi" class="mw-redirect" title="Euskaltel-Euskadi">Euskaltel-Euskadi</a> professional cycling team, partly sponsored by the Basque Government participated in the UCI World Tour division until 2014. Known for their orange tops and hill-climbing ability, their fans were famous for lining the famous Pyrenean climbs in the Tour de France, in support of their compatriots.\n</p><p>Each April the week-long <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_the_Basque_Country" title="Tour of the Basque Country">Tour of the Basque Country</a> showcases the beautiful rolling Basque countryside.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)#Politics" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country (greater region) \xc2\xa7&#160;Politics</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Giza_katea,_Urbia.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Giza_katea%2C_Urbia.JPG/220px-Giza_katea%2C_Urbia.JPG" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Giza_katea%2C_Urbia.JPG/330px-Giza_katea%2C_Urbia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Giza_katea%2C_Urbia.JPG/440px-Giza_katea%2C_Urbia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="930" data-file-height="615" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Giza_katea,_Urbia.JPG" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div><a href="/wiki/2014_human_chain_for_Basque_Country%27s_right_to_decide" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 human chain for Basque Country&#39;s right to decide">2014 human chain for Basque Country\'s right to decide</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gure_Esku_Dago_manifestazioa_%22Demokrazia%22_-_Bilbo_2017-09-16_-_9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Gure_Esku_Dago_manifestazioa_%22Demokrazia%22_-_Bilbo_2017-09-16_-_9.jpg/220px-Gure_Esku_Dago_manifestazioa_%22Demokrazia%22_-_Bilbo_2017-09-16_-_9.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Gure_Esku_Dago_manifestazioa_%22Demokrazia%22_-_Bilbo_2017-09-16_-_9.jpg/330px-Gure_Esku_Dago_manifestazioa_%22Demokrazia%22_-_Bilbo_2017-09-16_-_9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Gure_Esku_Dago_manifestazioa_%22Demokrazia%22_-_Bilbo_2017-09-16_-_9.jpg/440px-Gure_Esku_Dago_manifestazioa_%22Demokrazia%22_-_Bilbo_2017-09-16_-_9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1026" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gure_Esku_Dago_manifestazioa_%22Demokrazia%22_-_Bilbo_2017-09-16_-_9.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Demonstration in <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a> in solidarity with <a href="/wiki/Catalan_independence_referendum,_2017" title="Catalan independence referendum, 2017">Catalan independence referendum</a>, September 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>While there is no independent Basque state, Spain\'s <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous community</a> of the Basque Country, made up of the provinces of \xc3\x81lava (Araba), Biscay (Bizkaia) and Gipuzkoa, is primarily a historical consequence and an answer to the wide autonomy claim of its population.\n</p><p>Navarre has a separate statute of autonomy, a contentious arrangement designed during Spanish transition to democracy (the <i>Amejoramiento</i>, an \'upgrade\' of its previous status during dictatorship). It refers back to the kingdom status of Navarre (up to 1841) and their traditional institutional and legal framework (<a href="/wiki/Fuero#Basque_and_Pyrenean_fueros" title="Fuero">charters</a>). Basque, the original and main language of Navarre up to the late 18th century, has kept family transmission especially in the northern part of Navarre and central areas to a lesser extent, designated as Basque speaking or mixed area in Navarrese law. Questions of political, linguistic and cultural allegiance and identity are highly complex in Navarre. Politically some Basque nationalists would like to integrate with the Basque Autonomous Community.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/French_Basque_Country" title="French Basque Country">French Basque Country</a> today does not exist as a formal political entity and is officially simply part of the French <a href="/wiki/Department_(country_subdivision)" title="Department (country subdivision)">department</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es_Atlantiques" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es Atlantiques">Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es Atlantiques</a>, centered in <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9arn" title="B\xc3\xa9arn">B\xc3\xa9arn</a>. In recent years the number of mayors of the region supporting the creation of a separate Basque department has grown to 63.87%.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> So far, their attempts have been unsuccessful.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_conflicts">Political conflicts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Political conflicts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language_2">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque language</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)#Language" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country (greater region) \xc2\xa7&#160;Language</a></div>\n<p>Both the Spanish and French governments have, at times, suppressed Basque <a href="/wiki/Natural_language" title="Natural language">linguistic</a> and cultural identity. The <a href="/wiki/French_Republics_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="French Republics (disambiguation)">French Republics</a>, the epitome of the <a href="/wiki/Nation-state" class="mw-redirect" title="Nation-state">nation-state</a>, have a long history of attempting the complete cultural absorption of cultural minority groups. Spain has, at most points in its history, granted some degree of linguistic, cultural, and even political autonomy to its Basques, but under the <a href="/wiki/Spain_under_Franco" class="mw-redirect" title="Spain under Franco">regime of Francisco Franco</a>, the Spanish government reversed the advances of Basque nationalism, as it had fought in the opposite side of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>: cultural activity in Basque was limited to folkloric issues and the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>.\n</p><p>Today, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Basque_Country" title="Southern Basque Country">Southern Basque Country</a> within Spain enjoys an extensive cultural and political autonomy. The majority of schools under the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/Basque_education_system" title="Basque education system">Basque education system</a> use Basque as the primary medium of teaching. However, the situation is more delicate in the <a href="/wiki/French_Basque_Country" title="French Basque Country">Northern Basque Country</a> within France, where Basque is not officially recognized, and where lack of autonomy and monolingual public schooling in French exert great pressure on the Basque language.\n</p><p>In Navarre, Basque has been declared an endangered language, since the anti-Basque and conservative government of <a href="/wiki/Navarrese_People%27s_Union" title="Navarrese People&#39;s Union">Navarrese People\'s Union</a> opposes the symbols of Basque culture,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> highlighting a Spanish identity for Navarre.\n</p><p>Basque is also spoken by immigrants in the major cities of Spain and France, in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, in many parts of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, especially in Nevada, Idaho, and California.<sup id="cite_ref-Trask1997_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trask1997-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>1</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_status_and_violence">Political status and violence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Political status and violence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Muralbelfast2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Muralbelfast2.jpg/220px-Muralbelfast2.jpg" width="220" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Muralbelfast2.jpg/330px-Muralbelfast2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Muralbelfast2.jpg/440px-Muralbelfast2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="490" data-file-height="479" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Muralbelfast2.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>A republican mural in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> showing solidarity with <a href="/wiki/Basque_nationalism" title="Basque nationalism">Basque nationalism</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Since its articulation by Sabino Arana in the late 19th century, the more radical currents of <a href="/wiki/Basque_nationalism" title="Basque nationalism">Basque nationalism</a> have demanded the right of <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a> and even <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a>. Within the Basque country, this element of Basque politics is often in balance with the conception of the Basque Country as just another part of the Spanish state, a view more commonly espoused on the right of the political spectrum. In contrast, the desire for greater autonomy or independence is particularly common among <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">leftist</a> Basque nationalists. The right of self-determination was asserted by the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Parliament" title="Basque Parliament">Basque Parliament</a> in 2002 and 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\nSince self-determination is not recognized in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a>, a wide majority of Basques abstained (55%) and some even voted against it (23.5%) in the ratification referendum of December 6 of that year. However, it was approved by clear <a href="/wiki/Majority" title="Majority">majority</a> overall in Spanish (87%). The autonomous regime for the Basque Country was approved in a 1979 referendum but the autonomy of Navarre (<i>Amejoramiento del Fuero</i>: "improvement of the charter") was never subject to a referendum but only approved by the Navarrese Cortes (parliament).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_violence">Political violence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Political violence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Basque_conflict" title="Basque conflict">Basque conflict</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA (separatist group)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grupos_Antiterroristas_de_Liberaci%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Grupos Antiterroristas de Liberaci\xc3\xb3n">Grupos Antiterroristas de Liberaci\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Batall%C3%B3n_Vasco_Espa%C3%B1ol" title="Batall\xc3\xb3n Vasco Espa\xc3\xb1ol">Batall\xc3\xb3n Vasco Espa\xc3\xb1ol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comandos_Aut%C3%B3nomos_Anticapitalistas" title="Comandos Aut\xc3\xb3nomos Anticapitalistas">Comandos Aut\xc3\xb3nomos Anticapitalistas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iraultza" title="Iraultza">Iraultza</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small><i>(August 2010)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Classification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>As with their language, the Basques are clearly a distinct cultural group in their region. They regard themselves as culturally and especially linguistically distinct from their surrounding neighbours. Some Basques, especially in Spain, are strongly nationalist, identifying far more firmly as Basques than as citizens of any existing state. Others do not, feeling as much Basque as Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-Euskobar\xc3\xb3metro_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Euskobar\xc3\xb3metro-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Many Basques regard the designation as a "cultural minority" as incomplete, favouring instead the definition as a nation, the commonly accepted designation for the Basque people up to the rise of the nation-states and the definition imposed by the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Basque_people#Revolution_and_war" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Basque people">1812 Spanish Constitution</a>.\n</p><p>In modern times, as a European people living in a highly industrialized area, cultural differences from the rest of Europe are inevitably blurred, although a conscious cultural identity as a people or nation remains very strong, as does an identification with their homeland, even among many Basques who have emigrated to other parts of Spain or France, or to other parts of the world.\n</p><p>The strongest distinction between the Basques and their traditional neighbours is linguistic. Surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance-language</a> speakers, the Basques traditionally spoke (and many still speak) a language that was not only non-Romance but non-Indo-European. The prevailing belief amongst Basques, and forming part of their national identity, is that their language has continuity with the people who were in this region since not only pre-Roman and pre-Celtic times, but since the Stone Age.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetics">Genetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Genetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:06_laiatzen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/06_laiatzen.jpg/220px-06_laiatzen.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/06_laiatzen.jpg/330px-06_laiatzen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/06_laiatzen.jpg/440px-06_laiatzen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1694" data-file-height="1270" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:06_laiatzen.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div>Basque peasants <a href="/wiki/Laia_(tool)" title="Laia (tool)">ploughing</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1920, <a href="/wiki/H._G._Wells" title="H. G. Wells">H. G. Wells</a> referred to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_race" title="Mediterranean race">Mediterranean race</a> as the <i>Iberian race</i>. He regarded it as a fourth subrace of the Caucasian race, along with the <i>Aryan</i>, <i>Semitic</i>, and <i>Hamitic</i> subraces. He stated that the main <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> that most purely represented the racial stock of the Iberian race was the Basques, and that the Basques were the descendants of the <a href="/wiki/Cro-Magnons" class="mw-redirect" title="Cro-Magnons">Cro-Magnons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In 1994, in his book <i>The History and Geography of Human Genes</i>, <a href="/wiki/Population_geneticist" class="mw-redirect" title="Population geneticist">population geneticist</a> <a href="/wiki/L._Luca_Cavalli-Sforza" class="mw-redirect" title="L. Luca Cavalli-Sforza">L. Luca Cavalli-Sforza</a> stated that "there is support from many sides" for the hypothesis that the Basques are the descendants of the original Cro-Magnons.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:J%C3%B3venes_con_trajes_vascos_en_Zubieta_(1_de_3)_-_Fondo_Car-Kutxa_Fototeka.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/J%C3%B3venes_con_trajes_vascos_en_Zubieta_%281_de_3%29_-_Fondo_Car-Kutxa_Fototeka.jpg/220px-J%C3%B3venes_con_trajes_vascos_en_Zubieta_%281_de_3%29_-_Fondo_Car-Kutxa_Fototeka.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/J%C3%B3venes_con_trajes_vascos_en_Zubieta_%281_de_3%29_-_Fondo_Car-Kutxa_Fototeka.jpg/330px-J%C3%B3venes_con_trajes_vascos_en_Zubieta_%281_de_3%29_-_Fondo_Car-Kutxa_Fototeka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/J%C3%B3venes_con_trajes_vascos_en_Zubieta_%281_de_3%29_-_Fondo_Car-Kutxa_Fototeka.jpg/440px-J%C3%B3venes_con_trajes_vascos_en_Zubieta_%281_de_3%29_-_Fondo_Car-Kutxa_Fototeka.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="678" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:J%C3%B3venes_con_trajes_vascos_en_Zubieta_(1_de_3)_-_Fondo_Car-Kutxa_Fototeka.jpg" class="internal" title="Meudaich"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Basque_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Basque people">Basque people</a> in 1927</div></div></div>\n<p>Even before the development of modern <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a> based on <a href="/wiki/DNA_sequencing" title="DNA sequencing">DNA sequencing</a>, Basques were already noted for distinctive genetic patterns, such as possessing the highest global apportion of the <a href="/wiki/Rh_blood_group_system" title="Rh blood group system">Rh-</a> blood type (35% phenotypically, 60% genetically). Additionally, the Basque population has virtually no <a href="/wiki/ABO_blood_group_system" title="ABO blood group system">B blood type</a>, nor the related AB type. They have a high rate of O blood group but this is probably due to isolation.\n</p><p>Although they are genetically distinctive in some ways, the Basques are still very typically European in terms of their <a href="/wiki/Y-DNA" class="mw-redirect" title="Y-DNA">Y-DNA</a> and <a href="/wiki/MtDNA" class="mw-redirect" title="MtDNA">mtDNA</a> sequences, and in terms of some other genetic <a href="/wiki/Locus_(genetics)" title="Locus (genetics)">loci</a>. These same sequences are widespread throughout the western half of Europe, especially along the western fringe of the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-Dupanloup2004_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dupanloup2004-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pericic2005_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pericic2005-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The distinctiveness noted by studies of \'classical\' genetic markers (such as blood groups) and the apparently "pre-Indo-European" nature of the Basque language has resulted in a popular and long-held view that Basques are "living fossils" of the earliest <a href="/wiki/Anatomically_modern_humans" class="mw-redirect" title="Anatomically modern humans">modern humans</a> who colonized Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Alonso2005_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alonso2005-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> However, studies of the <a href="/wiki/Y-chromosome" class="mw-redirect" title="Y-chromosome">Y-chromosome</a> found that on their direct male lineages, the vast majority of modern Basques have a common ancestry with other Western Europeans, namely a marked predominance of <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_R1b_(Y-DNA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup R1b (Y-DNA)">Haplogroup R1b</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Alonso2005_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alonso2005-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Initially Haplogroup R1b was theorised to be that a Palaeolithic marker, introduced when Europe was repopulated after the <a href="/wiki/Last_Glacial_Maximum" title="Last Glacial Maximum">Last Glacial Maximum</a>, about 25,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> As such, Basque populations were used as proxy representatives for the "Palaeolithic component" in admixture studies that tried to quantify the extent of Neolithic diffusions. Such studies concluded that the main components in the European genomes appear to derive from ancestors whose features were similar to those of modern Basques and people of the <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a> (or Western Asia), with average values greater than 35% for both these parental populations, regardless of whether molecular information is taken into account or not. The smallest degree of both Basque and Near Eastern admixture is found in Finland, whereas the highest values are, respectively, 70% "Basque" in Spain and roughly 60% "<a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near Eastern</a>" in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dupanloup2004_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dupanloup2004-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p.1365 Table 3</span>)</sup> This theory encountered inconsistencies even prior to most recent chronological re-evaluations. That R1b should be a Palaeolithic marker was an <i>ad hoc</i> assumption suggested by Semino <i>et al.</i> (2000) and propagated by subsequent scholars without further analysis. Higher resolution <a href="/wiki/STR_analysis" title="STR analysis">STR analysis</a> of R1b lineages from other western European populations (e.g. Italy<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> or Britain (Wales))<sup id="cite_ref-Alonso2005_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alonso2005-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> show that their populations appear to derive from the Basque ones.\n</p><p>More recent studies instead propose that R1b spread through Europe from southwest Asia in the Neolithic period or later, between 4,000 and 8,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-Balaresque_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Balaresque-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crawford2007_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crawford2007-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Myres2010_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Myres2010-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sj\xc3\xb6din2011_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sj\xc3\xb6din2011-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Autosome" title="Autosome">Autosomal genetic</a> studies have confirmed that Basques share:\n</p>\n<ul><li>close genetic ties to other <a href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" class="mw-redirect" title="European ethnic groups">Europeans</a>, especially with <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spaniards</a>, who have a common genetic identity of over 70% with Basques.<sup id="cite_ref-Dupanloup2004_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dupanloup2004-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>homogeneity amongst both their Spanish and French populations, according to high-density SNP genotyping study done in May 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-Dupanloup2004_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dupanloup2004-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and;</li>\n<li>a genomic distinctiveness, relative to other European populations.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Several ancient DNA samples have been recovered and amplified from Palaeolithic sites in the Basque region. The collection of mtDNA haplogroups sampled there differed significantly compared to their modern frequencies. The authors concluded that there is "discontinuity" between ancient and modern Basques.<sup id="cite_ref-jogg.info_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jogg.info-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Thus, while Basques harbour some very archaic lineages (such as mtDNA Hg U8a),<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> they are not of "undiluted Palaeolithic ancestry", nor are they ancestral to large parts of western Europe. Rather, their genetic distinctiveness is a result of centuries of low population size, genetic drift and endogamy.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="New_genetic_findings.2C_2015"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_genetic_findings,_2015">New genetic findings, 2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: New genetic findings, 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2015, a new scientific study of Basque DNA was published which seems to indicate that Basques are descendants of <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> farmers who mixed with local <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> hunters before becoming genetically isolated from the rest of Europe for millennia.<sup id="cite_ref-thescientist_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thescientist-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Mattias Jakobsson from Uppsala University in Sweden analysed genetic material from eight Stone Age human skeletons found in El Portal\xc3\xb3n Cavern in <a href="/wiki/Atapuerca_Mountains" title="Atapuerca Mountains">Atapuerca</a>, northern Spain. These individuals lived between 3,500 and 5,500 years ago, after the transition to farming in southwest Europe. The results show that these early Iberian farmers are the closest ancestors to present-day Basques.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The official findings were published in <i>Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences</i> of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-G\xc3\xbcntherValdiosera2015_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G\xc3\xbcntherValdiosera2015-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> According to the study, the "results show that the Basques trace their ancestry to early farming groups from Iberia, which contradicts previous views of them being a remnant population that trace their ancestry to Mesolithic hunter-gatherer groups." These early Neolithic farmer ancestors of the Basques, however, additionally mixed with local southwestern hunter-gatherers, and "the proportion of hunter gatherer-related admixture into early farmers also increased over the course of two millennia." This admixed group was also found to be ancestral to other modern-day Iberian peoples, but while the Basques remained relatively isolated for millennia after this time, later migrations into Iberia led to distinct and additional admixture in all other Iberian groups.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It has also been suggested that the high incidence of R1b among Basques can be attributed to an invasion by <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans" title="Proto-Indo-Europeans">Indo-European</a> warriors who intermarried with local women, who then raised the resulting children in their culture, not that of their fathers.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_Basques">Notable Basques</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notable Basques">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Basques" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Basques">List of Basques</a></div>\n<p>Among the most notable Basque people are <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Elcano" title="Juan Sebasti\xc3\xa1n Elcano">Juan Sebasti\xc3\xa1n Elcano</a> (led the first successful expedition to circumnavigate the globe after <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a> died mid-journey); <a href="/wiki/Sancho_III_of_Navarre" class="mw-redirect" title="Sancho III of Navarre">Sancho III of Navarre</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Ignatius_of_Loyola" title="Ignatius of Loyola">Ignatius of Loyola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francis_Xavier" title="Francis Xavier">Francis Xavier</a>, founders of the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a>. <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Gardoqui" title="Diego de Gardoqui">Don Diego Mar\xc3\xada de Gardoqui y Arriquibar</a> (1735\xe2\x80\x931798) was Spain\'s first Ambassador to the United States. <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Unamuno" title="Miguel de Unamuno">Miguel de Unamuno</a> was a noted novelist and philosopher of the late 19th and the 20th century.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Basques&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation"
